Limitations

  • RAGTruth evidence spans are human review artifacts derived from answer-side annotations and source passages.
  • RAGTruth labels answer-side hallucination spans; source-side evidence spans require human mapping before span-localization claims.
  • External case-pack results validate this dataset and adapter path only; they are not general RAG-evaluation SOTA proof.
  • RAGTruth publishes response.jsonl and source_info.jsonl separately, joined by source_id.
  • labels are answer-side hallucination spans; expected_evidence_spans require human curation before span-overlap claims.
  • good-quality rows without hallucination spans map to no_failure_detected; span-labeled rows map to partial_support or contradicted_answer.
  • stratified samples are deterministic and should record sample_size, sample_seed, and stratify_by fields before review.

| " The individual members of the fraternity will likely be considered private individuals, and not public figures; the latter have a harder time proving defamation. | The Supreme Court has been clear on the issue of libelous statements about the government: The government cannot sue for defamation. | " Brian Stelter: Fraternity to 'pursue all available legal action' The next question is:. | A private person suing for defamation must establish that the defendant has published a false factual statement that is about the person and that it also harms the person's reputation. | A plaintiff in a defamation case must show that the statements were "of or concerning" the plaintiff. | The private plaintiff also must show that the defendant knew that the statement was false, or believed it was true but lacked a reasonable basis, or acted negligently in checking the facts. | " "Actionable" means the statement must be both false and defamatory. | Kollman that "the elements of libel are (1) publication of (2) an actionable statement with (3) the requisite intent. | There are strict rules about who can be a plaintiff in a defamation action like this. | The UVA situation is not your run-of-the-mill defamation case. | Defamatory statements about a group are therefore not actionable by the group's individual members, for the most part. | When the statements are about a group without naming an individual, it's hard to say the statement is "concerning" the individual -- and groups generally cannot sue. | A fraternity is not an individual, but a group. | It sounds obvious, but if you're going to say a statement hurt you, you have to prove the statement actually was about you to begin with. | True statements cannot be defamatory. | Like all rules, however, there are exceptions. | Neither can pure statements of opinion, because they theoretically cannot be either true or false.
